Status: `FULL_REPLAY_PASS; FRESH_CORRECTION_REVIEW_PENDING`

Maximum conclusion:
`BOUNDED_POINTWISE_JOINT_INVARIANT_SUBSPACE_ATLAS_CHARACTERIZED`.

## Result first

The corrected atlas, complete only for its nine named pointwise families, finds a sharp hierarchy
rather than a blanket negative.

Smaller metric/phi families often **do** carry a unique real central `2+2` split: 11,983 family rows
across 5,210 configurations. Each has primary-block ranks `1;1;2`; the rank-two block comes from a
complex-conjugate spectral pair whose combined real plane is canonical. Another 2,225 rows have four
real lines and therefore three competing `2+2` pairings.

But none of those unique smaller-family splits survives the complete curvature orchestra. The full
Riemann-plus-phi and Weyl-plus-phi families generate the full four-dimensional matrix algebra in
5,760 of 6,144 configurations, including every configuration where a smaller family has a unique
split. Their only common invariant subspaces are therefore zero and the full tangent space. In the
remaining 384 configurations the joint algebra is scalar and supplies no distinguished plane.

The gradient-generated orbit is never two-dimensional, and neither the Riemann nor Weyl bivector
operator has an isolated real simple eigenbivector plane anywhere in the registered ensemble.

The bounded observation is therefore:

> Individual sections can organize themselves into a real `2+2` pattern, but the complete
> pointwise two-jet orchestra does not preserve that partition.

This does not rule out a distribution selected by transport, higher jets, global integrability,
finite-cell completion, boundary data, or time-live dynamics. None of those entered this audit.

## Complete bounded coverage

- Parent configurations: 6,144 = 48 carriers x 16 masks x 8 contexts.
- Registered operator families: nine.
- Original family classifications: 55,296.
- Nonlinear coordinate three-jet probes: two per configuration.
- Transformed configurations: 12,288.
- Nonlinear family comparisons: 110,592.
- Discarded configurations or classifications: zero.
- Non-uncertain nonlinear classification discordances: zero.
- Retained uncertain nonlinear comparisons: 24.
- Worst parent-tensor residual: zero.
- Worst nonlinear covariance residual: `2.2204460492503131e-16`.

The corrected independent verifier rebuilt the metric curvature, covariant phi-Hessian, nine named operator
families, commutants, central blocks, gradient orbits, bivector tests, and nonlinear coordinate jets
on 480 original and 960 transformed preregistered anchors. All 12,960 independent family
classifications agree with the atlas. It computes every anchor before reading saved builder
classifications and constructs real primary projectors by an independent Vandermonde/CRT method.
Four anchor comparisons fall in the registered uncertainty band and are retained. All ten exercised
catch-proofs reject their mutations.

## Joint-family findings

| family | generated-algebra dimensions | rank-two central result | gradient-orbit dimensions |
|---|---|---|---|
| Ricci | 1 on 768; 4 on 5,376 | unique on 4,298; three competing on 1,078 | 0/1/4 |
| phi Hessian | 1 on 3,072; 4 on 3,072 | unique on 3,003; three competing on 69 | 0/4 |
| phi dyad | 1 on 3,072; 2 on 3,072 | none | 0/1 |
| Ricci + Hessian | 1 on 384; 4 on 3,072; 16 on 2,688 | unique on 2,533; three competing on 539 | 0/4 |
| Ricci + Hessian + dyad | 1 on 384; 4 on 2,688; 16 on 3,072 | unique on 2,149; three competing on 539 | 0/4 |
| Riemann generators | 1 on 768; 16 on 5,376 | none | 0/1/4 |
| Weyl generators | 1 on 768; 16 on 5,376 | none | 0/1/4 |
| full Riemann joint | 1 on 384; 16 on 5,760 | none | 0/4 |
| full Weyl joint | 1 on 384; 16 on 5,760 | none | 0/4 |

Across the nine named families there are 11,983 unique and 2,225 multiple central `2+2` rows, and
zero two-dimensional gradient-generated orbits. The 11,983 unique rows occur in Ricci (4,298), phi
Hessian (3,003), Ricci-plus-Hessian (2,533), and Ricci-plus-Hessian-plus-dyad (2,149). Every one maps
to `FULL_MATRIX_ALGEBRA_IRREDUCIBLE` after either complete curvature family is added. The parent
gradient is zero in 3,072 configurations, spacelike in 2,304, and timelike in 768; no null-gradient
parent occurs in this ensemble.

## Curvature-eigenbivector findings

Both curvature operators yield zero isolated real simple eigenplanes in all 6,144 configurations.
The Weyl operator has six isolated complex eigenvalues in 5,376 configurations and a sixfold
repeated eigenvalue in 768. Riemann has a mixture of complex isolated spectra, 118 real but
non-simple eigenbivector cases, and 768 sixfold-repeated cases. No vector was selected from a
repeated eigenspace, and no non-simple bivector was misreported as a tangent plane.

## Nonlinear chart audit

Both registered nonlinear maps use the complete metric and scalar chain rule through coordinate
three-jets. Every non-uncertain algebra dimension, commutant/center dimension, central-block class,
gradient-orbit class, and bivector multiplicity is unchanged. The 24 near-threshold comparisons are
recorded in `NUMERIC_MARGIN_LEDGER.tsv`; none produces a unique split or supports a physical claim.

The first atlas pass is preserved. It produced 23,994 apparent nonlinear discordances because the
classifier diagonalized an arbitrary numerical representative of a repeated scalar center. The
resulting eigenspace basis was coordinate-dependent even though the invariant algebra was not.
Replacing that diagnostic with exact scalar-identity handling and polynomial spectral projectors
removed all non-uncertain discordances. `CLASSIFIER_CORRECTION.md` records the correction, and the
failed result and transcript remain historical evidence.

A second, more important correction was forced by the first fresh adversarial review. The corrected
scalar-center classifier still rejected complex spectra, missing real primary planes made by
complex-conjugate pairs and incorrectly supporting a zero-unique-split report. That failed review,
result, transcript, and family census are preserved. The current builder uses real polynomial
spectral projectors; the verifier uses a separately implemented Vandermonde/CRT construction. Both
recover the adversarial rank pattern `1;1;2` and agree on all independent anchors.

The second fresh review confirmed that census but found a further fail-closure defect: both
implementations treated an exact Lorentzian self-adjoint nilpotent Jordan operator as classified.
It also found that the implemented projector gate was `1e-7`, not the preregistered `1e-9`, and that
several catches used catch-only predicates. That failed review is preserved. The current builder and
independent verifier separately test semisimplicity of every primary cluster, mark the exact Jordan
counterexample uncertain, enforce `1e-9` on projector acceptance and stability, and pass the saved
registries, coverage, bivector census, uncertainty ledger, and result through the same validators
used by their mutations. The full replay reproduces the prior census; a new fresh correction review
is still required before final banking.

## What survives the audit

- `OBSERVED`, bounded and independently verified: four smaller named families produce 11,983 unique
  real central splits across 5,210 configurations.
- `OBSERVED`, bounded and independently verified: the complete Riemann-plus-phi and Weyl-plus-phi
  pointwise two-jet families are full-algebra irreducible on 5,760 configurations—including every
  smaller-family unique-split case—and fully ambiguous on the remaining 384.
- `OBSERVED`, bounded and independently verified: no registered gradient orbit or isolated real
  simple curvature eigenbivector supplies a two-plane.
- `OPEN`: whether transport, higher jets, integrability, global finite-cell closure, a boundary
  functional, or time-live structure selects a distribution.
- `OPEN`: any physical angular sector, action, source, carrier, boundary, scale, or bootstrap law.

## Caveats and premise audit

- This is complete only for the nine **named** preregistered pointwise families. Joint subsets such
  as `{R,D}`, `{H,D}`, and partial curvature-plus-phi combinations were not registered. It is not
  exhaustive over all subsets or all possible differential concomitants.
- The two nonlinear coordinate maps are finite probes, not a proof over the full diffeomorphism
  group.
- Central reducing subspaces are a strict selector test. Noncentral invariant flags are retained as
  ambiguity and are not promoted to preferred physical planes.
- Rank tolerance `1e-9`, eigenvalue clustering `1e-8`, and the `1e-11..1e-7` uncertainty band are
  numerical choices pinned by habit. All threshold-near rows are retained.
- No action, field equation, source, carrier, section, boundary, physical scale, topology, or
  evolution law was loaded.

## Four banking gates

1. Preregistered: **YES**, including the exact independently verified anchor set.
2. Full space or bounded scope justified: **YES** for all 6,144 configurations, nine registered
   families, and two nonlinear probes; not exhaustive beyond that pointwise two-jet scope.
3. Independently verified: **INTERNAL PASS** on 480 original and 960 nonlinear anchors with an
   independent real-primary implementation and ten catches. Two fresh reviews failed and forced
   preserved corrections; the post-Jordan fresh review remains required before final banking.
4. Every premise audited: **YES** in `PREMISE_STATUS_LEDGER.tsv`; the physical selector and all
   dynamical/global structures remain `OPEN`.

This is a bounded invariant-subspace atlas, not a physical section-selection theorem.
# Lay Report

We asked whether the nine named pointwise families in this atlas naturally divide the local
geometry into two special pairs of directions—without first telling them which directions we wanted.

Think of the metric, curvature, and phi field as an orchestra. Earlier maps showed that the
instruments interact. This audit asked a sharper question: does the music itself divide the
orchestra into two uniquely identifiable sections?

Across 6,144 local metric configurations, the corrected answer has two layers.

Individual sections really do organize themselves. Ricci curvature, the phi Hessian, and some of
their smaller combinations repeatedly divide the four directions into one real two-direction plane
and its two-direction complement. We found 11,983 such family cases. A fresh reviewer caught that
our first classifier had missed them because it treated a complex-conjugate mathematical pair as an
obstruction instead of combining it into a real plane.

Then the two registered full curvature-plus-phi families enter. When all of their curvature
directions play together with phi, every one of those smaller-family partitions is mixed back into
the four-dimensional space. In 5,760 configurations no nontrivial common section survives; in the
remaining 384 the named full families are too degenerate to choose one.

Three other possible shortcuts still fail inside this map:

- Following the direction in which phi changes never grew into exactly a two-dimensional section.
- Curvature never supplied one clean real plane through a unique simple eigen-pattern.
- Some smaller subsets produced multiple competing pairings. Others did produce a unique
  family-level pairing, but none of those pairings survived either registered full family.

We also rewrote a large independent sample in nonlinear coordinates. The underlying classifications
stayed the same to machine precision. A first numerical classifier falsely reported coordinate
changes because it chose arbitrary axes inside a degenerate space; that error was preserved,
diagnosed, fixed, and independently checked.

The useful insight is not “there is no angular geometry.” It is more interesting:

> Some instruments naturally make a `2+2` section, but neither registered full curvature-plus-phi
> family leaves that section alone. Within these named families, the full symphony is irreducibly
> four-dimensional.

That is a concrete clue: a physical angular sector, if UDT has one, is unlikely to be a pointwise
subspace preserved by every local curvature operator. It may instead be a transported, averaged, or
globally compatible pattern across a finite cell or time-live history. Those possibilities remain
open. This audit did not choose an action, boundary, carrier, or new mechanism.
# Classifier Correction — Repeated Central Eigenspace

The first complete build returned `VERIFICATION_REQUIRED` despite tensor covariance residual
`2.2204460492503131e-16`. It reported 23,994 nonlinear classification disagreements, all confined
to `central_block_ranks` and `central_block_status`; algebra dimension, commutant dimensions,
gradient-orbit dimensions/signatures, and reducibility class had zero disagreements.

Cause: the central-block routine diagonalized an arbitrary floating SVD representative even when
the metric-self-adjoint center was one-dimensional. That center contains only the scalar identity,
but numerical diagonalization chose an arbitrary eigenbasis in its repeated four-dimensional
eigenspace. Tiny basis-dependent complex components caused the same scalar center to alternate
between `4` and `COMPLEX_JORDAN_OR_NUMERIC_OBSTRUCTION` after a coordinate change.

Correction:

1. a one-dimensional self-adjoint center is classified directly as the scalar identity with one
   rank-four block;
2. higher-dimensional real central spectral projectors are constructed as polynomials in the
   central element, not from an arbitrary eigenvector matrix;
3. projector idempotence, metric self-adjointness, centrality, and operator commutation gates remain
   unchanged;
4. no family, configuration, tolerance, chart, or scientific classification target changed.

The failed result and transcript are preserved byte-for-byte as `PRECORRECTION_ATLAS_RESULT.json`
and `PRECORRECTION_ATLAS_TRANSCRIPT.txt` with SHA-256 values
`bf73dbdfd12c9b07bd167725c0f9086bdd9f9539b3c034793a4fca2ff5d6a93e` and
`975299fabd703fd34e6461c96c0502a8d63634250188f800a9ff4a822e3d07ef`.

The corrected complete replay has zero non-uncertain classification disagreements. Its 24
uncertain comparisons remain retained in `NUMERIC_MARGIN_LEDGER.tsv`.
# Independent-Verifier Implementation Corrections

Date: 2026-07-21

The independent verifier was implemented only after the main atlas had completed. Two execution
defects stopped its first attempts before a verification result was written:

1. A diagnostic-only Riemann bivector construction supplied one inverse metric to an `einsum` that
   explicitly required two. The corrected call raises both leading curvature indices, matching the
   independently implemented production bivector check.
2. The omitted-nonlinear-jet catch initially selected the first transformed anchor, whose phi
   gradient was zero. The omitted gradient-times-map-second-jet term was therefore exactly zero and
   made the negative control vacuous. The catch now selects the first preregistered anchor for which
   that contraction is nonzero and tests the raw scalar second-partial transformation directly.

Neither defect changed an atlas candidate, family, tolerance, saved row, scientific classifier, or
maximum conclusion. The completed pre-review verifier produced its result only after both
corrections and its then-registered catches passed.

A later fresh review exposed three substantive certification defects, now preserved in
`FRESH_ADVERSARIAL_CORRECTION_REVIEW.md`:

3. Product and CRT primary projectors did not first establish semisimplicity. Both implementations
   therefore called an exact Lorentzian self-adjoint nilpotent Jordan operator classified. They now
   use separately written algebraic-versus-geometric multiplicity gates and fail closed on defective
   or rank-ambiguous clusters.
4. Projector residual and stability acceptance used `1e-7`; both now enforce the registered `1e-9`.
5. Several negative controls used catch-only predicates. Saved registries, full row coverage,
   bivector summaries, uncertainty identities, and the result contract now pass through reusable
   validators, and their mutations pass through those same validators. The exact Jordan example is
   a tenth end-to-end catch.

The post-correction full builder and independent verifier reproduce the same census and pass all ten
catches. Fresh external review and repository-wide banking remain separate final gates.

   343	def bivector_operator_summary(operator: np.ndarray, metric: np.ndarray) -> dict[str, int | str]:
   344	    eig,vec=np.linalg.eig(operator)
   345	    used=set(); simple=[]; repeated=0;complex=0;uncertain=False
   346	    for i in range(6):
   347	        if i in used:continue
   348	        group=[j for j in range(6) if j not in used and abs(eig[i]-eig[j])<=CLUSTER*max(1.0,abs(eig[i]),abs(eig[j]))];used.update(group)
   349	        if len(group)>1: repeated+=len(group);continue
   350	        if abs(eig[i].imag)>CLUSTER or np.max(np.abs(vec[:,i].imag))>CLUSTER:complex+=1;continue
   351	        v=vec[:,i].real;v/=np.linalg.norm(v);b01,b02,b03,b12,b13,b23=v;pf=abs(b01*b23-b02*b13+b03*b12)
   352	        gap=min(abs(eig[i]-eig[j])/max(1.0,abs(eig[i]),abs(eig[j])) for j in range(6) if j!=i)
   353	        uncertain|=LOW<=pf<=HIGH or LOW<=gap<=HIGH
   354	        if pf>TOL:continue
   355	        b=np.zeros((4,4))
   356	        for x,(a,c) in zip(v,PAIRS):b[a,c]=x;b[c,a]=-x
   357	        rank,ur,_=rank_info(b);uncertain|=ur
   358	        if rank!=2:continue
   359	        u,_,_=np.linalg.svd(b);basis=u[:,:2];gram=basis.T@metric@basis;ge=np.linalg.eigvalsh(0.5*(gram+gram.T));scale=max(1.0,float(np.max(np.abs(ge))));zero=int(np.count_nonzero(np.abs(ge)<=TOL*scale))
   360	        projector=None if zero else basis@np.linalg.inv(gram)@basis.T@metric
   361	        simple.append(projector)
   362	    nondeg=[p for p in simple if p is not None];pairs=sum(max(relmax(nondeg[i]+nondeg[j],np.eye(4)),relmax(nondeg[i]@nondeg[j],np.zeros((4,4))))<=TOL for i in range(len(nondeg)) for j in range(i+1,len(nondeg)))
   363	    return {"isolated_real_simple_eigenplanes":len(simple),"nondegenerate_simple_eigenplanes":len(nondeg),"complementary_split_count":pairs,"repeated_eigenvalue_multiplicity":repeated,"complex_isolated_count":complex,"numeric_status":"NUMERIC_UNCERTAIN" if uncertain else "NUMERIC_CLASSIFIED"}

   366	def bivector_summary(tensor: np.ndarray, inverse: np.ndarray, metric: np.ndarray) -> dict[str, int | str]:
   367	    raised=np.einsum("ae,bf,efcd->abcd",inverse,inverse,tensor)
   368	    operator=np.array([[raised[a,b,c,d] for c,d in PAIRS] for a,b in PAIRS])
   369	    return bivector_operator_summary(operator,metric)

   372	def multiply(left, right):
   373	    lv,lf,ls=left;rv,rf,rs=right
   374	    return lv*rv,lf*rv+lv*rf,ls*rv+lv*rs+np.outer(lf,rf)+np.outer(rf,lf)

   377	def transform_jets(g,dg,ddg,pv,pf,ps,j,k,ell):
   378	    gj=[[(j[mu,a],k[mu,a].copy(),ell[mu,a].copy()) for a in range(4)] for mu in range(4)]
   379	    gt=np.zeros((4,4));dgt=np.zeros((4,4,4));ddgt=np.zeros((4,4,4,4))
   380	    for a,b in itertools.product(range(4),repeat=2):
   381	        total=(0.0,np.zeros(4),np.zeros((4,4)))
   382	        for mu,nu in itertools.product(range(4),repeat=2):
   383	            comp=(g[mu,nu],np.einsum("r,rc->c",dg[:,mu,nu],j),np.einsum("rs,rc,sd->cd",ddg[:,:,mu,nu],j,j)+np.einsum("r,rcd->cd",dg[:,mu,nu],k))
   384	            total=tuple(x+y for x,y in zip(total,multiply(multiply(gj[mu][a],gj[nu][b]),comp)))
   385	        gt[a,b],dgt[:,a,b],ddgt[:,:,a,b]=total
   386	    pft=np.einsum("r,ra->a",pf,j);pst=np.einsum("rs,ra,sb->ab",ps,j,j)+np.einsum("r,rab->ab",pf,k)
   387	    return gt,dgt,ddgt,pv,pft,pst

   424	def classify_family(operators: list[np.ndarray], gradient: np.ndarray, metric: np.ndarray) -> dict[str, object]:
   425	    algebra, algebra_info = associative_algebra(operators)
   426	    commutant, commutant_rank, commutant_residual = centralizer(operators)
   427	    center, center_rank, center_residual = center_of_commutant(commutant)
   428	    selfcenter, selfcenter_rank, selfcenter_residual = selfadjoint_center(center, metric)
   429	    blocks = central_block_decomposition(operators, metric, commutant, center, selfcenter)
   430	    orbit = krylov_orbit(operators, gradient, metric)
   431	    uncertain = bool(
   432	        algebra_info["uncertain"] or commutant_rank.uncertain or center_rank.uncertain
   433	        or selfcenter_rank.uncertain or orbit["uncertain"]
   434	        or blocks["status"].startswith("NUMERIC_UNCERTAIN")
   435	    )
   436	    if algebra_info["dimension"] == DIM * DIM:
   437	        reducibility = "FULL_MATRIX_ALGEBRA_IRREDUCIBLE"
   438	    elif blocks["rank2_split_count"] == 1:
   439	        reducibility = "UNIQUE_CENTRAL_2PLUS2"
   440	    elif blocks["rank2_split_count"] > 1:
   441	        reducibility = "MULTIPLE_CENTRAL_2PLUS2"
   442	    elif len(commutant) > len(center):
   443	        reducibility = "PROPER_ALGEBRA_NONCENTRAL_AMBIGUITY"
   444	    else:
   445	        reducibility = "PROPER_ALGEBRA_NO_CENTRAL_2PLUS2"
   446	    return {
   447	        "operator_count": len(operators),
   448	        "nonzero_operator_count": len(normalize_operators(operators)),
   449	        "algebra_dimension": algebra_info["dimension"],
   450	        "algebra_iterations": algebra_info["iterations"],
   451	        "algebra_closure_residual": algebra_info["closure_residual"],
   452	        "commutant_dimension": len(commutant),
   453	        "commutant_residual": commutant_residual,
   454	        "commutant_center_dimension": len(center),
   455	        "center_residual": center_residual,
   456	        "selfadjoint_center_dimension": len(selfcenter),
   457	        "selfadjoint_center_residual": selfcenter_residual,
   458	        "central_block_ranks": blocks["block_ranks"],
   459	        "central_rank2_split_count": blocks["rank2_split_count"],
   460	        "central_block_status": blocks["status"],
   461	        "central_projector_residual": blocks["projector_residual"],
   462	        "central_projector_stability_residual": blocks["stability_residual"],
   463	        "gradient_orbit_dimension": orbit["dimension"],
   464	        "gradient_orbit_metric_rank": orbit["metric_rank"],
   465	        "gradient_orbit_signature": orbit["signature"],
   466	        "gradient_orbit_closure_residual": orbit["closure_residual"],
   467	        "gradient_orbit_projector_residual": orbit["projector_residual"],
   468	        "reducibility_class": reducibility,
   469	        "numeric_status": "NUMERIC_UNCERTAIN" if uncertain else "NUMERIC_CLASSIFIED",
   470	    }
   471	
   472	
   473	def weyl_tensor(metric: np.ndarray, riemann: np.ndarray, ricci: np.ndarray, scalar: float) -> np.ndarray:
   474	    result = np.zeros_like(riemann)
   475	    for a, b, c, d in itertools.product(range(DIM), repeat=4):
   476	        result[a, b, c, d] = (
   477	            riemann[a, b, c, d]
   478	            - 0.5 * (
   479	                metric[a, c] * ricci[b, d] - metric[a, d] * ricci[b, c]
   480	                - metric[b, c] * ricci[a, d] + metric[b, d] * ricci[a, c]
   481	            )
   482	            + scalar * (metric[a, c] * metric[b, d] - metric[a, d] * metric[b, c]) / 6.0
   483	        )
   484	    return result
   485

   487	def intrinsic_objects(geometry, phi_first: np.ndarray, phi_second: np.ndarray) -> dict[str, object]:
   488	    metric = geometry.metric
   489	    inverse = geometry.inverse
   490	    dphi = np.asarray(phi_first, dtype=float)

    57	def digest(path: Path) -> str:
    58	    value = hashlib.sha256()
    59	    with path.open("rb") as handle:
    60	        for block in iter(lambda: handle.read(131072), b""):
    61	            value.update(block)
    62	    return value.hexdigest()
    63

    65	def tsv(path: Path) -> list[dict[str, str]]:
    66	    with path.open(encoding="utf-8", newline="") as handle:
    67	        return list(csv.DictReader(handle, delimiter="\t"))

    70	def write_tsv(name: str, fields: list[str], rows: list[dict[str, object]]) -> None:
    71	    with (HERE / name).open("w", encoding="utf-8", newline="") as handle:
    72	        writer = csv.DictWriter(handle, fieldnames=fields, delimiter="\t", lineterminator="\n")
    73	        writer.writeheader()
    74	        writer.writerows(rows)

    77	def check_sources() -> list[dict[str, object]]:
    78	    rows = []
    79	    for relative, expected in SOURCE_HASHES.items():
    80	        path = ROOT / relative
    81	        actual = digest(path)
    82	        if actual != expected:
    83	            raise AssertionError(f"source manifest {relative}: {actual}")
    84	        rows.append({"path": relative, "sha256": actual, "role": "IMMUTABLE_SOURCE"})
    85	    for relative, expected in PREREG_HASHES.items():
    86	        path = HERE / relative
    87	        actual = digest(path)
    88	        if actual != expected:
    89	            raise AssertionError(f"preregistration {relative}: {actual}")
    90	        rows.append({"path": relative, "sha256": actual, "role": "PREREGISTRATION"})
    91	    return rows

    93	
    94	def operator_adjoint_residuals(objects: dict[str, object]) -> tuple[float, float]:
    95	    metric = np.asarray(objects["metric"])
    96	    self_residual = max(
    97	        relmax(np.asarray(objects[name]).T @ metric, metric @ np.asarray(objects[name]))
    98	        for name in ("R", "H", "D")
    99	    )
   100	    skew_residual = max(
   101	        relmax(operator.T @ metric, -metric @ operator)
   102	        for name in ("RG", "WG") for operator in objects[name]
   103	    )
   104	    return self_residual, skew_residual
   105	
   106	
   107	def family_rows(configuration_id: str, objects: dict[str, object]) -> list[dict[str, object]]:
   108	    rows = []
   109	    for family_id, keys in FAMILY_REGISTRY:
   110	        classification = classify_family(family_operators(objects, keys), np.asarray(objects["gradient"]), np.asarray(objects["metric"]))
   111	        rows.append({"configuration_id": configuration_id, "family_id": family_id, "operator_keys": ";".join(keys), **classification})
   112	    return rows
   113	
   114	
   115	def bivector_rows(configuration_id: str, objects: dict[str, object]) -> tuple[dict[str, object], list[dict[str, object]]]:
   116	    summary: dict[str, object] = {}
   117	    rows: list[dict[str, object]] = []
   118	    for name, key in (("RIEMANN", "riemann_down"), ("WEYL", "weyl_down")):
   119	        current, candidates = bivector_eigenplanes(name, np.asarray(objects[key]), np.asarray(objects["inverse"]), np.asarray(objects["metric"]))
   120	        for field, value in current.items():
   121	            summary[f"{name.lower()}_{field}"] = value
   122	        for index, candidate in enumerate(candidates):
   123	            rows.append({"configuration_id": configuration_id, "candidate_id": f"{name}_E{index:02d}", **candidate})
   124	    return summary, rows

   127	def expected_generator_residual(original_geometry, original_objects, transformed_objects, transform) -> float:
   128	    j = np.asarray(transform["J"], dtype=float)
   129	    inverse_j = np.linalg.inv(j)
   130	    maximum = 0.0
   131	    weyl_up = np.einsum("ar,rsuv->asuv", np.asarray(original_objects["inverse"]), np.asarray(original_objects["weyl_down"]))
   132	    for destination_index, (a, b) in enumerate(PAIRS):
   133	        expected_r = np.zeros((4, 4))
   134	        expected_w = np.zeros((4, 4))
   135	        for mu in range(4):
   136	            for nu in range(4):
   137	                expected_r += j[mu, a] * j[nu, b] * inverse_j @ original_geometry.riemann_up[:, :, mu, nu] @ j
   138	                expected_w += j[mu, a] * j[nu, b] * inverse_j @ weyl_up[:, :, mu, nu] @ j
   139	        maximum = max(
   140	            maximum,
   141	            relmax(transformed_objects["RG"][destination_index], expected_r),
   142	            relmax(transformed_objects["WG"][destination_index], expected_w),
   143	        )
   144	    return maximum
   145	
   146	
   147	def covariance_residual(original_geometry, original_objects, transformed_objects, transform) -> dict[str, float]:
   148	    j = np.asarray(transform["J"], dtype=float)
   149	    inverse_j = np.linalg.inv(j)
   150	    residuals = {
   151	        "metric": relmax(transformed_objects["metric"], j.T @ original_objects["metric"] @ j),
   152	        "gradient": relmax(transformed_objects["gradient"], inverse_j @ original_objects["gradient"]),
   153	        "ricci_operator": relmax(transformed_objects["R"], inverse_j @ original_objects["R"] @ j),
   154	        "hessian_operator": relmax(transformed_objects["H"], inverse_j @ original_objects["H"] @ j),
   155	        "phi_dyad": relmax(transformed_objects["D"], inverse_j @ original_objects["D"] @ j),
   156	        "curvature_generators": expected_generator_residual(original_geometry, original_objects, transformed_objects, transform),
   157	    }
   158	    residuals["maximum"] = max(residuals.values())
   159	    return residuals
   160

   374	
   375	def krylov_orbit(operators: list[np.ndarray], seed: np.ndarray, metric: np.ndarray) -> dict[str, object]:
   376	    ops = normalize_operators(operators)
   377	    vector = np.asarray(seed, dtype=float)
   378	    if float(np.linalg.norm(vector)) <= ZERO_TOL:
   379	        return {
   380	            "dimension": 0, "signature": "ZERO_SEED", "metric_rank": 0,
   381	            "uncertain": False, "closure_residual": 0.0, "projector_residual": 0.0,
   382	        }
   383	    candidates = [vector]
   384	    previous = -1
   385	    uncertain = False
   386	    basis = np.zeros((DIM, 0))
   387	    while True:
   388	        columns = []
   389	        for item in candidates:
   390	            norm = float(np.linalg.norm(item))
   391	            if norm > ZERO_TOL:
   392	                columns.append(item / norm)
   393	        matrix = np.column_stack(columns)
   394	        u, _, _ = np.linalg.svd(matrix, full_matrices=False)
   395	        rank_result = numerical_rank(matrix)
   396	        uncertain |= rank_result.uncertain
   397	        basis = u[:, : rank_result.rank]
   398	        if rank_result.rank == previous or rank_result.rank == DIM:
   399	            break
   400	        previous = rank_result.rank
   401	        candidates = [basis[:, index] for index in range(basis.shape[1])]
   402	        candidates.extend(operator @ basis[:, index] for operator in ops for index in range(basis.shape[1]))
   403	    closure = max((float(np.linalg.norm(operator @ basis - basis @ (basis.T @ operator @ basis))) for operator in ops), default=0.0)
   404	    negative, positive, zero, gram_eigenvalues = subspace_signature(basis, metric)
   405	    metric_rank = negative + positive
   406	    signature = f"N{negative}_P{positive}_Z{zero}"
   407	    projector_residual = 0.0
   408	    if metric_rank == basis.shape[1]:
   409	        gram = basis.T @ metric @ basis
   410	        projector = basis @ np.linalg.inv(gram) @ basis.T @ metric
   411	        projector_residual = max(
   412	            relmax(projector @ projector, projector),
   413	            relmax(projector.T @ metric, metric @ projector),
   414	            max((relmax(projector @ operator, operator @ projector) for operator in ops), default=0.0),
   415	        )
   416	    scale = max(1.0, float(np.max(np.abs(gram_eigenvalues))) if gram_eigenvalues.size else 0.0)
   417	    uncertain |= bool(np.any((np.abs(gram_eigenvalues) >= UNCERTAINTY_LOW * scale) & (np.abs(gram_eigenvalues) <= UNCERTAINTY_HIGH * scale)))
   418	    return {
   419	        "dimension": basis.shape[1], "signature": signature, "metric_rank": metric_rank,
   420	        "uncertain": uncertain, "closure_residual": closure, "projector_residual": projector_residual,
   421	    }
   422	
   423	
   424	def classify_family(operators: list[np.ndarray], gradient: np.ndarray, metric: np.ndarray) -> dict[str, object]:
   425	    algebra, algebra_info = associative_algebra(operators)
   426	    commutant, commutant_rank, commutant_residual = centralizer(operators)
   427	    center, center_rank, center_residual = center_of_commutant(commutant)
   428	    selfcenter, selfcenter_rank, selfcenter_residual = selfadjoint_center(center, metric)
   429	    blocks = central_block_decomposition(operators, metric, commutant, center, selfcenter)
   430	    orbit = krylov_orbit(operators, gradient, metric)
   431	    uncertain = bool(
   432	        algebra_info["uncertain"] or commutant_rank.uncertain or center_rank.uncertain
   433	        or selfcenter_rank.uncertain or orbit["uncertain"]
   434	        or blocks["status"].startswith("NUMERIC_UNCERTAIN")
   435	    )
   436	    if algebra_info["dimension"] == DIM * DIM:
   437	        reducibility = "FULL_MATRIX_ALGEBRA_IRREDUCIBLE"
   438	    elif blocks["rank2_split_count"] == 1:
   439	        reducibility = "UNIQUE_CENTRAL_2PLUS2"
   440	    elif blocks["rank2_split_count"] > 1:
   441	        reducibility = "MULTIPLE_CENTRAL_2PLUS2"
   442	    elif len(commutant) > len(center):
   443	        reducibility = "PROPER_ALGEBRA_NONCENTRAL_AMBIGUITY"
   444	    else:
   445	        reducibility = "PROPER_ALGEBRA_NO_CENTRAL_2PLUS2"
   446	    return {
   447	        "operator_count": len(operators),
   448	        "nonzero_operator_count": len(normalize_operators(operators)),
   449	        "algebra_dimension": algebra_info["dimension"],
   450	        "algebra_iterations": algebra_info["iterations"],
   451	        "algebra_closure_residual": algebra_info["closure_residual"],
   452	        "commutant_dimension": len(commutant),
   453	        "commutant_residual": commutant_residual,
   454	        "commutant_center_dimension": len(center),
   455	        "center_residual": center_residual,
   456	        "selfadjoint_center_dimension": len(selfcenter),
   457	        "selfadjoint_center_residual": selfcenter_residual,
   458	        "central_block_ranks": blocks["block_ranks"],
   459	        "central_rank2_split_count": blocks["rank2_split_count"],
   460	        "central_block_status": blocks["status"],
   461	        "central_projector_residual": blocks["projector_residual"],
   462	        "central_projector_stability_residual": blocks["stability_residual"],
   463	        "gradient_orbit_dimension": orbit["dimension"],
   464	        "gradient_orbit_metric_rank": orbit["metric_rank"],
   465	        "gradient_orbit_signature": orbit["signature"],
   466	        "gradient_orbit_closure_residual": orbit["closure_residual"],
   467	        "gradient_orbit_projector_residual": orbit["projector_residual"],
   468	        "reducibility_class": reducibility,
   469	        "numeric_status": "NUMERIC_UNCERTAIN" if uncertain else "NUMERIC_CLASSIFIED",
   470	    }
   471	
   472	
   473	def weyl_tensor(metric: np.ndarray, riemann: np.ndarray, ricci: np.ndarray, scalar: float) -> np.ndarray:
   474	    result = np.zeros_like(riemann)
   475	    for a, b, c, d in itertools.product(range(DIM), repeat=4):
   476	        result[a, b, c, d] = (
   477	            riemann[a, b, c, d]
   478	            - 0.5 * (
   479	                metric[a, c] * ricci[b, d] - metric[a, d] * ricci[b, c]
   480	                - metric[b, c] * ricci[a, d] + metric[b, d] * ricci[a, c]
   481	            )
   482	            + scalar * (metric[a, c] * metric[b, d] - metric[a, d] * metric[b, c]) / 6.0
   483	        )
   484	    return result
   485	
   486	
   487	def intrinsic_objects(geometry, phi_first: np.ndarray, phi_second: np.ndarray) -> dict[str, object]:
   488	    metric = geometry.metric
   489	    inverse = geometry.inverse
   490	    dphi = np.asarray(phi_first, dtype=float)
   491	    ddphi = np.asarray(phi_second, dtype=float)
   492	    gradient = inverse @ dphi
   493	    hessian = ddphi.copy()
   494	    for a, b in itertools.product(range(DIM), repeat=2):
   495	        hessian[a, b] -= sum(geometry.christoffel[rho, a, b] * dphi[rho] for rho in range(DIM))
   496	    ricci_operator = inverse @ geometry.ricci
   497	    hessian_operator = inverse @ hessian
   498	    dyad = np.outer(gradient, dphi)
   499	    weyl = weyl_tensor(metric, geometry.riemann_down, geometry.ricci, geometry.scalar_curvature)
   500	    riemann_generators = [geometry.riemann_up[:, :, a, b].copy() for a, b in PAIRS]
   501	    weyl_up_first = np.einsum("ar,rsuv->asuv", inverse, weyl)
   502	    weyl_generators = [weyl_up_first[:, :, a, b].copy() for a, b in PAIRS]
   503	    return {
   504	        "metric": metric,
   505	        "inverse": inverse,
   506	        "gradient": gradient,
   507	        "dphi": dphi,
   508	        "hessian_cov": hessian,
   509	        "R": ricci_operator,
   510	        "H": hessian_operator,
   511	        "D": dyad,
   512	        "RG": riemann_generators,
   513	        "WG": weyl_generators,
   514	        "riemann_down": geometry.riemann_down,
   515	        "weyl_down": weyl,
   516	    }
   517	
   518	
   519	def family_operators(objects: dict[str, object], keys: tuple[str, ...]) -> list[np.ndarray]:
   520	    result: list[np.ndarray] = []
   521	    for key in keys:
   522	        value = objects[key]
   523	        if isinstance(value, list):
   524	            result.extend(value)
   525	        else:
   526	            result.append(np.asarray(value, dtype=float))
   527	    return result
   528	
   529	
   530	def bivector_operator(tensor_down: np.ndarray, inverse: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
   531	    raised = np.einsum("ae,bf,efcd->abcd", inverse, inverse, tensor_down)
   532	    return np.asarray([[raised[a, b, c, d] for c, d in PAIRS] for a, b in PAIRS], dtype=float)
   533	
   534	
   535	def bivector_matrix(vector: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
   536	    result = np.zeros((DIM, DIM))
   537	    for value, (a, b) in zip(vector, PAIRS):
   538	        result[a, b] = value
   539	        result[b, a] = -value
   540	    return result
   541	
   542	
   543	def plane_projector(bivector: np.ndarray, metric: np.ndarray) -> tuple[np.ndarray | None, str, float]:
   544	    u, singular, _ = np.linalg.svd(bivector)
   545	    rank_result = numerical_rank(bivector)
   546	    if rank_result.rank != 2:
   547	        return None, "NOT_RANK_TWO", 0.0
   548	    basis = u[:, :2]
   549	    negative, positive, zero, eigenvalues = subspace_signature(basis, metric)
   550	    signature = f"N{negative}_P{positive}_Z{zero}"
   551	    if zero:
   552	        return None, signature, float(np.min(np.abs(eigenvalues)))
   553	    gram = basis.T @ metric @ basis
   554	    projector = basis @ np.linalg.inv(gram) @ basis.T @ metric
   555	    return projector, signature, float(np.min(np.abs(eigenvalues)))

   558	def bivector_eigenplanes(
   559	    tensor_name: str, tensor_down: np.ndarray, inverse: np.ndarray, metric: np.ndarray
   560	) -> tuple[dict[str, object], list[dict[str, object]]]:
   561	    operator = bivector_operator(tensor_down, inverse)
   562	    eigenvalues, eigenvectors = np.linalg.eig(operator)
   563	    used = set()
   564	    clusters: list[list[int]] = []
   565	    for start in range(len(eigenvalues)):
   566	        if start in used:
   567	            continue
   568	        cluster = []
   569	        for other in range(len(eigenvalues)):
   570	            if other in used:
   571	                continue
   572	            scale = max(1.0, abs(eigenvalues[start]), abs(eigenvalues[other]))
   573	            if abs(eigenvalues[start] - eigenvalues[other]) <= CLUSTER_TOL * scale:
   574	                cluster.append(other)
   575	        used.update(cluster)
   576	        clusters.append(cluster)
   577	    rows = []
   578	    projectors = []
   579	    repeated = 0
   580	    complex_count = 0
   581	    uncertain = False
   582	    for cluster in clusters:
   583	        if len(cluster) != 1:
   584	            repeated += len(cluster)
   585	            continue
   586	        index = cluster[0]
   587	        value = eigenvalues[index]
   588	        vector = eigenvectors[:, index]
   589	        gap = min(
   590	            (abs(value - eigenvalues[other]) / max(1.0, abs(value), abs(eigenvalues[other])) for other in range(len(eigenvalues)) if other != index),
   591	            default=float("inf"),
   592	        )
   593	        if abs(value.imag) > CLUSTER_TOL or np.max(np.abs(vector.imag)) > CLUSTER_TOL:
   594	            complex_count += 1
   595	            continue
   596	        real = vector.real
   597	        real /= max(float(np.linalg.norm(real)), ZERO_TOL)
   598	        b01, b02, b03, b12, b13, b23 = real
   599	        pfaffian = b01 * b23 - b02 * b13 + b03 * b12
   600	        simplicity = abs(float(pfaffian)) / max(float(np.dot(real, real)), ZERO_TOL)
   601	        if UNCERTAINTY_LOW <= simplicity <= UNCERTAINTY_HIGH or UNCERTAINTY_LOW <= gap <= UNCERTAINTY_HIGH:
   602	            uncertain = True
   603	        if simplicity > RANK_TOL:
   604	            continue
   605	        bivector = bivector_matrix(real)
   606	        projector, signature, metric_margin = plane_projector(bivector, metric)
   607	        if UNCERTAINTY_LOW <= metric_margin <= UNCERTAINTY_HIGH:
   608	            uncertain = True
   609	        row = {
   610	            "tensor": tensor_name,
udt_joint_invariant_subspace_atlas_2026-07-21/verify_repository_gates.py:113:        or result["gradient_generated_plane_rows"] != 0 or result["unique_bivector_complementary_split_rows"] != 0

   140	    result = []
   141	    for value in values:
   142	        norm = float(np.linalg.norm(value))

   243	def validate_package_manifest(repo: Path, corrupt: bool = False) -> dict[str, object]:
   244	    manifest = repo / PACKAGE / "SHA256SUMS.txt"
   245	    replay = run(manifest.parent, ["sha256sum", "--check", manifest.name])
   246	    if corrupt or replay.returncode or "FAILED" in replay.stdout:
